    "text": " Yes \u2014 the pattern you're describing tells us a lot. Getting 50, then 20, then hitting a wall suggests Reddit's rate limit is based on a **sliding window** (probably 100 requests per 10 minutes), and we're burning through it too fast even at 2 seconds per request.\n\nThe current approach is wrong in a fundamental way \u2014 we're treating rate limiting as an exception to recover from, when we should be **staying under the limit proactively** so we never hit it in the first place.\n\nHere's what I'd propose:\n\n**Smaller batches, longer rests.** Instead of 50 items then a 15 second pause, do **25 items then a 3 minute pause**. Reddit's rate limit window is likely 10 minutes, so resting 3 minutes between batches of 25 keeps us well under the ceiling. Slower overall but no rate limit interruptions.\n\n**Longer base delay.** 2 seconds between requests = 30 requests/minute = burns through any reasonable limit fast. Bumping to **3.5 seconds** (\u224817 requests/minute) gives Reddit more breathing room.\n\n**Drop the rewind logic entirely.** If we never hit the rate limit, we never need to rewind. The whole backoff/retry machinery becomes unnecessary complexity.\n\nAt 3.5s per item with 3 minute pauses every 25 items, the math for 3000 items works out to roughly **5.5 hours total** \u2014 but it would run uninterrupted rather than getting stuck in backoff loops that could stretch indefinitely. Want me to rework it on that basis?",

  // 1 minute for first backoff\\nconst BACKOFF_MAX  = 300000;  // cap at 5 minutes regardless of how many retries\\n// Base delay between requests (ms)\\nconst BASE_DELAY = 2000;\\n// Batch size before a shorter mid-batch pause\\nconst BATCH_SIZE = 50;\\nconst BATCH_PAUSE = 15000; // 15 seconds between batches\\n\\nlet enrichStopped = false;\\n\\nasync function enrichAllItems(retryFailed = false) {\\n  if (state.enriching) return;\\n  enrichStopped = false;\\n\\n  // Decide which items to process:\\n  // Normal run: items where enriched is falsy\\n  // Retry run: items that were attempted (enrichAttempts > 0) but still have no title\\n  let toEnrich;\\n  if (retryFailed) {\\n    // Reset items that were previously stamped as done but have no useful data\\n    await db.items.toCollection().modify(item => {\\n      if (item.enriched && !item.title && !item.subreddit) {\\n        item.enriched = false;\\n      }\\n    });\\n    await loadData();\\n  }\\n\\n  const allItems = await db.items.toArray();\\n  toEnrich = allItems.filter(i => !i.enriched);\\n\\n  if (toEnrich.length === 0) {\\n    showToast('All items already enriched \\u2713', 'success');\\n    return;\\n  }\\n\\n  state.enriching = true;\\n  state.enrichProgress = { done: 0, total: toEnrich.length, enriched: 0, failed: 0, rateLimited: 0 };\\n  render();\\n\\n  let enrichedCount = 0;\\n  let failedCount = 0;\\n  let consecutiveFails = 0;\\n  let backoffCount = 0;     "type": "text",
    "text": " Good questions \u2014 let me address both.\n\n## Deduplication\n\nYes, we're already deduplicating on import. Both the CSV import and the Supabase sync check `where('redditId').equals(...)` before inserting, so the same post can't appear twice. However there's one gap: **the sync and the CSV import use different code paths**, so if you synced from Reddit first and then imported a CSV, or vice versa, duplicates could theoretically slip through if a `redditId` got stored slightly differently (e.g. with/without a `t3_` prefix). Worth a quick check \u2014 how many items do you have in the database right now vs what you'd expect?\n\n## Dead Items \u2014 Suggestions\n\nFor items that failed enrichment permanently, there are a few approaches with different tradeoffs:\n\n**Option A \u2014 \"Dead\" status flag** \u2014 add an `enrichStatus` field with values like `pending`, `enriched`, `dead`. Dead items stay in the database but are filtered out of browse/search by default, with an option to show them. This is the least destructive approach and keeps your item count honest.\n\n**Option B \u2014 Soft delete** \u2014 add a `deleted` boolean. Dead items get hidden everywhere but remain in IndexedDB and Supabase, recoverable if needed.\n\n**Option C \u2014 Hard delete** \u2014 remove them from the database entirely after a certain number of failed attempts. Simple and clean but irreversible.\n\n**Option D \u2014 Dead items folder** \u2014 automatically move them into a system folder called \"\u26b0\ufe0f Unavailable\" so they're segregated but browseable. Fits the existing folder metaphor.\n\nMy recommendation would be **Option A combined with D** \u2014 mark them with a status, auto-move them to a system folder, and exclude them from the default browse view. That way your main library stays clean but nothing is permanently lost. You could also add a bulk-delete action on that folder once you're confident you don't need them.\n\nWhich direction feels right to you?",
    "citations": []
  }

    "start_timestamp": "2026-03-04T15:14:54.129473Z",
    "stop_timestamp": "2026-03-04T15:15:05.000624Z",
    "flags": null,
    "type": "text",
    "text": " Currently it depends on *why* no data was found:\n\n- **Explicit 404/403** (`unavailable`) \u2192 marked `enriched: true`, `enrichStatus: 'dead'` immediately, no retries\n- **null response** (network error, empty JSON, silent rate limit) \u2192 `enrichAttempts` incremented, stays `pending` until it hits `MAX_ITEM_ATTEMPTS` (3), then marked `dead`\n\nThe problem with that second path is that a rate-limited item and a genuinely dead item look identical from the outside \u2014 both return null. So an item that failed purely due to rate limiting could get marked `dead` after 3 attempts even though the post is perfectly fine.\n\nNow that we have a clean `enrichStatus` model, the better approach would be:\n\n- **Explicit 404/403** \u2192 `dead` immediately, no retries (server told us definitively it's gone)\n- **null / no data** \u2192 stays `pending`, `enrichAttempts` incremented, **never automatically marked dead**\n- Dead status is **only ever set by an explicit server response**, not by a failure count\n\nThis means the retry run becomes the natural mechanism for cleaning up null failures rather than the attempt counter. Items that are truly dead will eventually return a 404/403 and get marked properly. Items that were just rate-limited will succeed on a retry.\n\nThe tradeoff is that genuinely broken items (malformed URLs, Reddit oddities that never return 404) would stay `pending` forever. We could handle that with a separate manual \"give up on these\" action rather than an automatic counter \u2014 keeping the automatic `dead` path reserved for definitive server responses only.\n\nDoes that logic feel right, or would you still want some attempt ceiling as a safety net?",
    "citations": []
  }
